        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>There's a lot to like about Revere, but almost none of the reasons center around his bat. Casual fans love his infectious smile and work ethic, which is nothing to say of his highlight-reel catches in the outfield as well. He was considered a signability pick by the Twins in the 2007 draft, picked just ahead of Rick Porcello by the Detroit Tigers, and wasn't ever projected to hit like he did in the minors. He managed to hit .326/.385/.408 in the minors, and his legend grew largely on the heels of his 2008 season in Beloit. Still, his .267/.310/.309 MLB line in 2011 tells us a little more about whether he'll get the bat knocked out of his hands at this level, so despite his stellar defense in the outfield, his ceiling will always be limited unless he develops either a knack for walking, or a bit more of a line-drive approach to enhance his extra-base capabilities. With a 96.2 percent contact rate in 2011, it's surprising he didn't find more gaps, and that's why it's a bit worrisome for his future. (Brandon Warne)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Keep an eye on Twins spring training, as Revere may get a shot to play every day somewhere in the Twins outfield. Revere should keep a pretty good batting average and excellent stolen-base rates, which would make him a nice pickup. He also may score his share of runs, because if Span is out, Revere will likely hit at the top of the lineup. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>You take the good, you take the bad, you take them both and there you have the Ben Revere. The good Revere is a scintillating defender in centerfield, making highlight-reel plays on an almost nightly basis. The good Revere is also among the game's best at making contact: he did so on over 97% of pitches that were in the strike zone in 2012. That Revere also puts the ball on the ground about five times as often as he does in the air, good for using his otherworldly speed to beat out tons of infield hits. He is also an adept base thief, something which should only improve hitting atop of the Phillies order. But the bad Revere is still scary. The bad Revere doesn't even have warning track power. The bad Revere's career wOBA is .287. His OPS .642. The bad Revere rarely takes a walk, and has a throwing arm so bad it would make Juan Pierre and Johnny Damon blush. Revere did get better at quickening his release, and he gets to the ball as good as anyone. But his value is almost solely tied to baserunning and defense, so if either slumps, he could be a total zero. In the National League, however, he should still rack up a ton of stolen bases, making him a very attractive fantasy play. (Brandon Warne)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Ben Revere, your new fantasy Juan Pierre. Actually, pretty much your new real-life Juan Pierre, too.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Revere has a specific skill-set which makes him more valuable in fantasy than in real life. He can do two things really well; hit for about .300 every year, and steal a ton of bases. He's not a big walker, instead relying on a contact-heavy approach. Due to his speed, he's been able to post higher than normal batting averages on balls in play thus far. That should continue, provided his fractured foot has healed over the offseason. The average and speed will play, but there's no reason to reach for him unless your league heavily weighs those two skills. He probably won't even hit a single home run this year. (<a href="https://twitter.com/Chris_Cwik">Chris Cwik</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Revere does two things really well. That has value in fantasy leagues, but there's no reason to reach for Revere.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Theres no mystery to Ben Revere. He has essentially solved pitchers of the same handedness for this stage of his career and produces some live drives and a ton of ground balls in order to hit for average (.294 or better in each of the last three seasons), even as league-wide hitting has declined. He runs (101 stolen bases in 126 attempts, same period; fourth in majors with 49 in 2014). He doesnt take free passes (5.2% to 4.8% to 2.1% from 2012 to 2014) and therefore is highly unlikely to approach 100 runs scored, even if the rest of his statistical lineup is good. Drive in runs? Forget it. Hit home runs? Ha! Thankfully, for fantasy purposes, his team seems to be committed to him in center field. Revere has more than enough athleticism to salvage his defensive value, which has nosedived thanks in part to his poor judgment and bad routes, at least. Whether that happens matters little in rotisserie and head-to-head circles in the short term, though. Hes a much more valuable player in fantasy than real life and is, basically, at peak performance age. Health isnt a major concern, but he did have relatively minor offseason ankle surgery. He, thus, comes with the usual two-category-player caveat, all eggs in one basket and such. Coming off a high-earnings year, hell be costly, thanks to the likely less discerning crowd. (Nicholas Minnix)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Revere has abilities to hit for average and run that are well above-average, making him a very useful player in fantasy leagues. Hes also a limited one coming off a high-earnings campaign, and the year-to-year price index for such a type seems to fluctuate much more than is justifiable.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Ben Revere is a classic "way better in fantasy than in real baseball player." It is not that he is terrible in real baseball. He rarely walks and hits for basically no power (four career home runs in 2660 major league plate appearances), but he runs the bases well and puts the ball on the bat often enough to manage above average on-base percentages. While there are questions about his defense in center field, hey, he's still a center fielder in name at least. So if one squints hard enough, Revere can look like a roughly average major league player in real baseball. No squinting is required in fantasy, though. Especially in category leagues. Revere has an average better than .300 the past three seasons, not surprising given his speed and ability to make contact, and that sort of batting average is very valuable in leagues that use it as a category. Revere has also averaged more than 30 steals a season since becoming a regular with the Twins in 2011. Another big win for fantasy owners in category leagues. The Nationals traded Drew Storen for him in the off-season, and while nothing is set in stone yet, it sounds like they plan to have Revere hit lead off. Even if he does not manage 150 or more games as he did the previous two seasons, hitting first will help his counting stats. Revere's usefulness in points leagues depends on the league setup. In categories leagues, especially traditional 4x4 and 5x5 leagues, Revere's ability to 30 or even 40 bases make him a starting outfielder in itself. When you figure in his high batting average as well as steals, he's at least as solid starter in any outfield. In NL-only 4x4 and 5x5 leagues, he is borderline good. Ah, steals and average.Yes, we are talking about that Ben Revere. (Matt Klaassen)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>In real baseball (and sabermetrically-oriented fantasy leagues), Ben Revere is useful. In traditional fantasy baseball, particularly NL-only leagues, Revere's steals and batting average make him borderline elite.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Ben Revere hit .305, .306, and .306 in 2013, 2014, and 2015, but an oblique injury led to a forgettable 2016 season with the Nationals in which he hit just .217 and lost his starting job to rookie sensation Trea Turner. Reveres entire game is built around speed. He was third in baseball with 176 stolen bases between 2011 and 2015 behind only Dee Gordon and Rajai Davis, and even his consistently high batting average is built on speed. His 62.8 percent groundball rate over the same period trailed only Everth Cabrera among qualified hitters. This is all a long way of me saying that I think Revere is an excellent bounce-back candidate. Revere is still just 28 years old, his oblique injury is behind him, and his one-year prove-it deal with the Angels affords him an excellent opportunity to regain a starting job behind often-injured Cameron Maybin in left field. Even if Revere settles into more of a platoon role as a fourth outfielder, Revere hits from the good side of the platoon, and he has the speed to contribute even in limited playing time. Revere has fallen from a top 150 player to undrafted, but I dont view him as a different player than he was a year ago. I think hes an excellent late-round flier. (Scott Spratt)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>An oblique injury led to the worst year in Ben Reveres career in 2016, but he is still young and landed in a good situation to bounce back. Expect a .300 batting average and 20 steals in a part-time role with the Angels with the upside for 40 steals if he regains a starting job.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>

        hideSO('so5');

        }
        else {
            panelo.style.display = 'none';
            document.getElementById('soa5').style.fontWeight = 'normal';
        }
    }

    function setAverage(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_average') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

    // Create the tooltips only on document load
    $(document).ready(function () {
        // Make sure to only match links to wikipedia with a rel tag
        $('a[tipgloss]').each(function () {
            // We make use of the .each() loop to gain access to each element via the "this" keyword...
            $(this).qtip(
		{
		    content: {
		        // Set the text to an image HTML string with the correct src URL to the loading image you want to use
		        text: " ",
		        ajax: {
		            url: $(this).attr('tipgloss') // Use the rel attribute of each element for the url to load
		        }
		    },
		    position: {
		        viewport: $(window),
		        at: "top center",
		        my: "bottom center",
		        effect: false
		    },
		    show: {
		        event: "click mouseenter",
		        solo: true // Only show one tooltip at a time
		    },
		    hide: {
		        event: "click mouseleave",
		        delay: 1000,
		        fixed: true
		    },
		    style: {
		        classes: "qtip-light"
		    }
		})

            // Make sure it doesn't follow the link when we click it
        });
    });
